  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6fd00105-fc17-4e21-a471-7d6185e4f94a'
      });

The US release changed the location from the UK to Connecticut, which I feel makes the w<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The author is from the UK and the UK version is the original. The US release changed the location from the UK to Connecticut, which I feel makes the whole thing jarring because the people do not behave or speak like Americans at all. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2799915334" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2799915334" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2799915334?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik?shelf=i-m-intrigued">i-m-intrigued</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2799915334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5791028328696306781">APPLAUSE! APPLAUSE! APPLAUSE! One of the quickest, one of the best crazy roller coaster experiences I had as soon as I took this book into my hands. Still shaky, blubbering (I already requested a translator to communicate properly), nail-less, confused, dizzy but also smiling and happy! GAVE MY FIVE FULL MYSTERIOUS SHINING STARS! <br/><br/>GREAT STORY TELLING, ATTENTION TAKER PLOT, FANTASTIC CHARACTERIZATION, FAST AND HEART THROBBING PACING AND GREAT-SATISFYING ENDING! What are you waiting for guys? The b</span>
  <span id="freeText5791028328696306781" style="display:none">APPLAUSE! APPLAUSE! APPLAUSE! One of the quickest, one of the best crazy roller coaster experiences I had as soon as I took this book into my hands. Still shaky, blubbering (I already requested a translator to communicate properly), nail-less, confused, dizzy but also smiling and happy! GAVE MY FIVE FULL MYSTERIOUS SHINING STARS! <br /><br />GREAT STORY TELLING, ATTENTION TAKER PLOT, FANTASTIC CHARACTERIZATION, FAST AND HEART THROBBING PACING AND GREAT-SATISFYING ENDING! What are you waiting for guys? The book is NOT going to fall from the sky and drop on your lap! Go and buy it and send me thank you letters for my encouraging words!<br /><br />We have an amazing heroine, Pippa (don’t confuse her with longstocking) Fitz-Amobi loves to search, pry, dig into, talented, smart, nerdy, funny, social, friendly, brave, stands between Nancy Drew and Veronica Mars, older version of Harriet Walsh, with her technical skills, tattoo-less and leather-less, chain-less version of Lisbeth Salander and a younger version Molder-less and alien nation-less version of Dana Scully!<br /> <br /> Blurb is tempting, amazing, intriguing makes you dive in, clasp the book into your fingers and never let it go as I did. My dogs are jealous of the book by barking to the moon to protest me. But I resumed my reading because it was gripping, hooking you from the first page kind of book.<br /> <br /> Five years ago, Andie Bell got missing and presumed dead by Sal Singh who committed suicide and sent a text message confessing his crime before he’d killed himself. But Andie’s body had never been found. The case is close! But Pippa is determined to open it by starting her own investigation process to write her school project and she firstly knocked Sal’s family door to ask an interview with his 20 years old brother Ravi who naturally becomes partners in crime with her and their project which turns out the mission for proving Sal’s innocence and finding who might have killed Andie!<br /> <br /> As they start to dig more, the person of interest list of Pippa becomes longer, includes Pippa’s best friend’s sister. <br /><br /> There are too many questions screaming inside your head: <br /><br /> Who really killed Andie? Or Andie is really dead? Did she deserve her ending? Because as soon as we learn more about her, we discover she is a bully, drama queen, drug dealer, blackmailer! Her amazing attributes gave me itchy fists to punch her. (It’s strange because I never wanted to kick presumed dead person or I’m not sure she is dead person! Well, that’s a first because this character is living, breathing -or not- scumbag!)<br /><br /> Who put the blame on Sal? Or Sal really did it? Well, he’s portrait of nice, humble, angelic guy made me call him Castiel as like Supernatural’s angel character. But we can sense he has been hiding something. His friends changed their testimonies about his where beings and his leaving time from their place and rejected to be his alibis. So where was he at the murder time?<br /><br /> Who was sending threatening messages to Pippa to stop her digging?<br /><br /> Well, I made one of my fastest reads and my spider sense didn’t work properly to find the killer or killers till the last pages. The author was always ten steps ahead of me! I’m so blessed to be beaten by her smart writing. I had great time to visualize this as a great YA mystery movie or limited Netflix series! (Anything could be better to replace the third season of 13 reasons why which could be named as 13 reasons of list why the hell did you shoot the third season!!!)<br /><br /> It was moving, enjoyable, nail biter, mind bending, surprisingly exciting, satisfying read. I enjoyed every page, every clue, every thrilling moments of this book. I highly recommend it! It was even better than One of Us is lying! <br /><br />And the best news is there are 3 more sequels to come out! I already started my excitement dance which is between Beyonce- All the single ladies moves and Staying Alive-Travolta moves. Yay!<br /><br /><a href="https://niluferozmekik.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/nilylovestoread/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a><br /><a href="https://www.facebook.com/nilufer.ozmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/NiluferOzmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781984896360" href="/book/show/45874065-a-good-girl-s-guide-to-murder">review of another edition</a>

      <a href="/user/show/59359185-random-house-reader-s-circle-rhrc">Random House Reader&#39;s Circle (RHRC)</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=bookstagram-made-me-do-it">bookstagram-made-me-do-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3124606116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8959040203571704438"><b>Surprise! I was asked to write the recommendation for this story on the Book of the Month website, and I'm thrilled to finally be able to share it with you as it's live on the site. If you'd like to go directly to the page, you can click <a href='https://www.bookofthemonth.com/all-books/young-adult/a-good-girls-guide-to-murder-635' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a>, just keep scrolling below if you are outside of the US and not a subscriber. </b><br/><br/>As a reader who developed her book obsession by devouring every Nancy Drew installment in elementary school, I've been an avid enthusiast of YA crime fiction for most of my life. </span>
  <span id="freeText8959040203571704438" style="display:none"><b>Surprise! I was asked to write the recommendation for this story on the Book of the Month website, and I'm thrilled to finally be able to share it with you as it's live on the site. If you'd like to go directly to the page, you can click <a href="https://www.bookofthemonth.com/all-books/young-adult/a-good-girls-guide-to-murder-635" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>, just keep scrolling below if you are outside of the US and not a subscriber. </b><br /><br />As a reader who developed her book obsession by devouring every Nancy Drew installment in elementary school, I've been an avid enthusiast of YA crime fiction for most of my life. I cannot resist a good mystery, and am always on the hunt for the next "it" book in the genre. I'm a busy mom of two, so it is rare for me to find a book so special that I can finish it in two sittings, but that's exactly what I found with <i>A Good Girl's Guide to Murder</i>.<br /><br />Pippa Fitz-Amobi is a true-crime-loving teen who aspires to become a top-notch journalist one day. So naturally, she decides to focus her senior capstone project on her small town's most buzzworthy, unsolved crime: the murder of Andie Bell. What begins as a simple proposal quickly turns into an in-depth investigation full of unexpected twists and turns. After teaming up with the alleged murderer's brother, the pair spiral into a web of danger and obsession, and quickly wonder if they've gotten themselves in too deep.<br /><br />This debut reads as if you are investigating alongside the main characters, and fans of true crime podcasts will rejoice in the multimedia formatting that so wittily engages the reader from beginning to end. If you enjoy a grounded, engaging mystery that features a diverse cast, discussions surrounding racial injustice, and the importance of found family, I cannot recommend this book highly enough. Whether you are aged 13 or 102, this book is for you!<br /><br /><i>*Many thanks to the publisher for providing my review copy.</i></span>

<div id="review_2943978612" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2943978612" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2943978612?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781984896360" href="/book/show/45874065-a-good-girl-s-guide-to-murder">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48328025-megs-bookrack?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2943978612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16872390316801711175">You heard it here first. I have found a new <b>favorite YA Mystery/Thriller</b>.<br/><br/>I am so stoked and clearly, absolutely loved, <i>A Good Girl's Guide to Murder</i>!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1586870881ra/29290249.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>For her Senior Capstone Project, Pippa Fitz-Amboi, an extraordinarily focused high school girl, decides to solve a murder.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495468538ra/22819798.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The disappearance and murder in question, that of Andie Bell, happened five years ago in Pippa's hometown. <br/><br/>The police, and thus everyone else, say the crime was committed by Andie's boyfriend, Sal Singh.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587053357ra/29303029.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Their biggest piece of evi</span>
  <span id="freeText16872390316801711175" style="display:none">You heard it here first. I have found a new <b>favorite YA Mystery/Thriller</b>.<br><br>I am so stoked and clearly, absolutely loved, <i>A Good Girl's Guide to Murder</i>!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1586870881ra/29290249.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For her Senior Capstone Project, Pippa Fitz-Amboi, an extraordinarily focused high school girl, decides to solve a murder.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495468538ra/22819798.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The disappearance and murder in question, that of Andie Bell, happened five years ago in Pippa's hometown. <br><br>The police, and thus everyone else, say the crime was committed by Andie's boyfriend, Sal Singh.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587053357ra/29303029.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Their biggest piece of evidence, a purported confession Sal texted his parents, days after Andie disappeared. This confession was sent just prior to Sal's own apparent suicide.<br><br>In spite of this, Pippa does not believe Sal is guilty. Andie's body was never recovered and there is no real physical evidence against him.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587053357ra/29303033.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Pippa is such a great character. She's an overachiever who works tirelessly towards her goal.<br><br>You can tell, once she sets her sights on something, she does not give up and that's exactly how she tackles this project.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587053357ra/29303030.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think one of the things that connected me so much to this story was Pippa. I found her super relatable and loved reading from her perspective.<br><br>She ends up befriending Sal's younger brother, Ravi, and that additional commitment to him, and clearing Sal's name, makes her even more steadfast in her project; even in the face of very real danger.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587053357ra/29303032.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Additionally, the format of this was creative and engaging. Using mixed media sources, including the transcripts from Pippa's multiple investigatory interviews, and a present day narrative, made me feel like I was a part of the investigation.<br><br>As Pippa is evaluating what she has learned along the way, she recaps things, as you actually would if you were working on this type of project; including a running list of current suspects and a murder board.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587053357ra/29303031.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The stakes were high and there were times Pippa was very legitimately in danger. Through it all, she stayed true to herself and fought hard to find justice for Andie and Sal.<br><br>I loved this so much, as I said. I could go on for many more paragraphs of all the positive attributes of this story, but don't just take my word for it, PICK THIS UP!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1563885266ra/27872800.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you love it even half as much as I did, you're in for a good time!<br><br>Well done by Holly Jackson. I am so excited to get more mysteries from her!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16872390316801711175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3196841832" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3196841832" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3196841832?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30978160-meredith?shelf=overdrive">overdrive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3196841832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16455232000897924406"><b>SMART GIRLS RULE!<br/><br/><i>A Good Girl’s Guide to Murder is a smart YA mystery/thriller about a 17-year-old girl who investigates a murder that rocked her small town 5 years ago. </i></b><br/><br/>Pippa “Pip” Fitz- Amobbi to conduct her Senior Capstone project on the disappearance of Andie Bell, a high school senior who was presumed to be murdered by her boyfriend, Sal Singh. Shortly after Andie went missing, Sal killed himself and confessed to her murder. But Andie’s body was never found. Convicted by the town and the pre</span>
  <span id="freeText16455232000897924406" style="display:none"><b>SMART GIRLS RULE!<br /><br /><i>A Good Girl’s Guide to Murder is a smart YA mystery/thriller about a 17-year-old girl who investigates a murder that rocked her small town 5 years ago. </i></b><br /><br />Pippa “Pip” Fitz- Amobbi to conduct her Senior Capstone project on the disappearance of Andie Bell, a high school senior who was presumed to be murdered by her boyfriend, Sal Singh. Shortly after Andie went missing, Sal killed himself and confessed to her murder. But Andie’s body was never found. Convicted by the town and the press, Sal’s name is permanently marred and his family is viewed as the town pariahs. To determine if Sal really was guilty, Pip uses her intelligence and quick wit, to examine multiple angles and threads that were overlooked by the police. This is not a conventional class project, and while it seems a little over the top in the beginning, Pip’s character approaches it in a way that makes sense.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“If a villain can be made, then he can be unmade.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Pip makes for a great heroine. She is intelligent and strong and has the knack for seeing things that others ignore. A self-identified nerd, you can’t help but root for her. She also is very much 17 years old and a little naive to the ways of the world. I would compare her to a softer version of Veronica Mars. <br /><br /> I was a little apprehensive from the start because I am not a huge fan of Young Adult novels, but this one worked for me. In the beginning, I was constantly thinking “what’s a 17 year old going to find that the police did not.” However, once it became clear that there were gaps in the police investigation that Pip was able to see, I was sold. Also, Pip’s approach to solving the case and getting people to talk about Andie and Sal, etc. helped solidify that this book was the real deal and not just about a kid who happens to luck into solving a crime. Jackson takes a multimodal approach to share Pip’s investigation; the narrative switches from the third person to interview recordings to pages in a diary to email exchanges, which kept it interesting and added an element of realism. <br /><br /><b>While I was a little hesitant to read this, I was so glad I did. I quickly became immersed in the narrative, wound up loving Pip’s character, and enjoyed the plot--I figured out the murderer very early on, but there were a few twists that threw me for a loop. </b>I look forward to seeing where Pip’s crime-solving skills lead her in the next book in the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16455232000897924406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3217089923" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3217089923" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3217089923?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3217089923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15126521521275833513">You know the feeling when you literally sit in the car outside your office and race to finish your book? That's what happened to me this morning with Holly Jackson's excellent debut novel, <b>
  <i>A Good Girl's Guide to Murder</i>
</b>.<br/><br/>“...I don’t know who I am when I’m not working, when I’m not focused on or totally consumed by a task. Who am I between the projects and the assignments, when there’s nothing to do? I haven’t found her yet as it scares me. Maybe that’s why, for my senior capstone project this </span>
  <span id="freeText15126521521275833513" style="display:none">You know the feeling when you literally sit in the car outside your office and race to finish your book? That's what happened to me this morning with Holly Jackson's excellent debut novel, <b>
  <i>A Good Girl's Guide to Murder</i>
</b>.<br /><br />“...I don’t know who I am when I’m not working, when I’m not focused on or totally consumed by a task. Who am I between the projects and the assignments, when there’s nothing to do? I haven’t found her yet as it scares me. Maybe that’s why, for my senior capstone project this year, I decided to solve a murder.”<br /><br />The murder of Andie Bell rocked Pippa Fitz-Amobi’s small New England town five years ago. She was pretty and popular, and when her boyfriend killed himself shortly after she disappeared, the case quickly closed, even if Andie’s body was never found.<br /><br />But for some reason, Pippa has always felt some nagging sense that the case wasn’t as cut and dry as it appeared. She thinks everyone was too quick to accuse Sal, Andie’s boyfriend, of the crime, even if all signs pointed to his guilt.<br /><br />When she decides to focus on the case as her senior capstone project, she doesn’t have any expectations of turning up new evidence, finding new suspects, or stirring up chaos, but all of those things occur. She also puts herself and her family in danger, especially as she stumbles closer and closer to answers to some unresolved questions.<br /><br />How far should she go? She can’t seem to stop, especially because she wants to prove Sal’s innocence to his younger brother, Ravi, who becomes her partner of sorts. But just what is the truth? And who will it hurt if it is revealed?<br /><br />This book was so good!! Even though I predicted some stuff (and as per usual, treated everyone like a potential suspect), I couldn’t get enough of this mystery. I really liked Pippa and Ravi, and I was completely hooked on the story, which had lots of twists and turns. Plus, how cool of a name is Pippa Fitz-Amobi?<br /><br />Trigger warning: some implied animal cruelty, although it happens outside the narrative.<br /><br />So glad this one was worth the hype, and can't wait to see what Jackson does next.<br /><br />Check out my list of the best books I read in 2019 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2019.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2019.html</a>. <br /><br />Check out my list of the best books of the decade at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/my-favorite-books-of-decade.html" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/my-favorite-books-of-decade.html</a>.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />Follow me on Instagram at <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener"> https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/.</a></span>

<div id="review_3308461399" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3308461399" />
    <a title="Arini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39722464-arini"><img alt="Arini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565922259p2/39722464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3308461399?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arini" href="/user/show/39722464-arini">Arini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/43969445-a-good-girl-s-guide-to-murder">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3308461399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14544764082980051773"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>A Good Girl’s Guide to Murder</i> is a BRILLIANT young adult whodunit mystery thriller about a senior year student, <b>Pippa Fitz Amobi</b>, who decides to ‘re-investigate’ a closed murder case that took place five years prior for her final Capstone Project. I want to stress that the audiobook is absolutely <b>spectacular</b>. It’s narrated full casts complete with cool background music and other accompanying sounds.<br/><br/>The book has a <b>unique formatting</b>. It’s written in journal-like entries decorated with new</span>
  <span id="freeText14544764082980051773" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><i>A Good Girl’s Guide to Murder</i> is a BRILLIANT young adult whodunit mystery thriller about a senior year student, <b>Pippa Fitz Amobi</b>, who decides to ‘re-investigate’ a closed murder case that took place five years prior for her final Capstone Project. I want to stress that the audiobook is absolutely <b>spectacular</b>. It’s narrated full casts complete with cool background music and other accompanying sounds.<br /><br />The book has a <b>unique formatting</b>. It’s written in journal-like entries decorated with newspaper clippings, charts, text screenshots, and interview recordings. During your reading, you’ll feel like you’re right there solving the crime alongside Pippa. <u>The first half of the book is repetitive</u> as it mostly contains transcripts of Pippa’s interview with people whom the victim had close relationships with.<br /><br />This book is full of plot twists. Some of it predictable, but <u>there’s shocking revelations in its predictability</u> that will keep you on your toes. Outside of the murder mystery, you’ll get <u>an inside scoop to Pippa’s personal life</u>—her loving relationship with her family and her hanging out with her best friends. Not to mention, <u>Pippa’s newfound love which is developing so subtly</u> you can barely tell this book has romance.<br /><br />Overall, I enjoyed this book. Distinguished as the format may be, I think I just don’t do well with this kind of ‘styling’. The story didn’t capture my FULL attention until I got to the second half. I think this book is too YA for my taste which I’m aware this is a ME problem. I mean, I can admit it’s well written and impressively clever. However, I also couldn’t help but want something <i>more</i>...intense and terrorizing.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>(Read as an Audiobook)</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14544764082980051773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3165581839" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3165581839" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6351259-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557692775p2/6351259.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3165581839?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/6351259-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781984896360" href="/book/show/45874065-a-good-girl-s-guide-to-murder">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6351259-michelle?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6351259-michelle?shelf=feb-2020-reads">feb-2020-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3165581839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16685633461295540360">I'm going to review this book the only way I know how. It's getting TWO ratings. Let's discuss:<br/><br/><b>3 stars</b> is where I stand on this book. It was good. It fell victim to my problem with YA (which is why I don't really read a lot of YA). I have so much trouble relating to the characters because that time in my life is long over and I have trouble caring. There were also some similarities to the murder being investigated and the first Serial Podcast case, so that kind of irked me a little. (I might be </span>
  <span id="freeText16685633461295540360" style="display:none">I'm going to review this book the only way I know how. It's getting TWO ratings. Let's discuss:<br /><br /><b>3 stars</b> is where I stand on this book. It was good. It fell victim to my problem with YA (which is why I don't really read a lot of YA). I have so much trouble relating to the characters because that time in my life is long over and I have trouble caring. There were also some similarities to the murder being investigated and the first Serial Podcast case, so that kind of irked me a little. (I might be being a little too picky on that one, but that's me being honest.)<br /><br /><b>4 stars</b> is what I think I would rate this if I didn't have a YA problem. I think it's unfair for me to leave out feedback on how I thought this was a good effort for YA and deserves much praise. It just wasn't for this particular reader and I don't want my late 30's take to ruin someone picking it up who really adores YA. For a younger reader, I think this book will be extremely popular and provides a good snapshot to life as a late teen.<br /><br /><b>Back to my 3 star review:</b> I got to page 60 and wanted to DNF. There were so many of my book friends who just raved so I had to keep going to see who did it. What bothered me a lot throughout the book was that the characters needed some fleshing out. Particularly Pippa. What a great girl character, but it was so one dimensional. She was a wonderful student, very devoted to this project, loved her family, but that was kind of it. I needed more why about her and I wanted to care more about her as a person. Most of the characterization seemed all very token high school crowd. I just wanted to be more emotionally invested in this than I was so that left me feeling disappointed. There was also a lot of repetition.<br /><br /><b>The four star:</b> I really liked the use of mixed media in here - the transcriptions, emails, text messages and charts. That was cool and helped the reader really feel like they were Pippa investigating this in real time. I complained about the repetition above, but for a younger reader I felt this served a good purpose in helping to see critical thinking skills at work. <br /><br />Overall, a very mixed bag and I doubt I will read the next book, but I'm glad that this is a winner among so many other people. I hope my review did a good job of bridging both sides since a YA book shouldn't have that held against it just because I don't really like to read them. That seems kind of unfair, don't you think?<br /><br />Thanks to the Buffalo Library for coming to my rescue and providing this copy at the peak of it's hype on the gram!<br /><br />Review Date: 02/10/2020<br />US Publication Date: 02/04/2020</span>

<div id="review_3330513127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3330513127" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3330513127?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781984896360" href="/book/show/45874065-a-good-girl-s-guide-to-murder">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=tres-annoying">tres-annoying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3330513127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer82620672639192399">Well, it appears, I've been reading YA mysteries all wrong these past years. Evidently, I should not expect plausibility, believability, character development or strong motivations in these books, like I do when reading adult mysteries. No wonder there is only ONE teen mystery that I think is good, and actual teens don't even like reading it, from what I hear. (It's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34810320.Sadie' title='Sadie by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sadie</a> in case you were wondering). <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40916679.A_Good_Girl_s_Guide_to_Murder__A_Good_Girl_s_Guide_to_Murder___1_' title='A Good Girl's Guide to Murder (A Good Girl's Guide to Murder, #1) by Holly Jackson' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Good Girl's Guide to Murder</a> starts off as a Serial rip-off, with upstanding Pippa swooping in </span>
  <span id="freeText82620672639192399" style="display:none">Well, it appears, I've been reading YA mysteries all wrong these past years. Evidently, I should not expect plausibility, believability, character development or strong motivations in these books, like I do when reading adult mysteries. No wonder there is only ONE teen mystery that I think is good, and actual teens don't even like reading it, from what I hear. (It's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34810320.Sadie" title="Sadie by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Sadie</a> in case you were wondering). <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40916679.A_Good_Girl_s_Guide_to_Murder__A_Good_Girl_s_Guide_to_Murder___1_" title="A Good Girl's Guide to Murder (A Good Girl's Guide to Murder, #1) by Holly Jackson" rel="nofollow noopener">A Good Girl's Guide to Murder</a> starts off as a Serial rip-off, with upstanding Pippa swooping in Sarah Koenig-like to clear the name of a poor brown guy accused of the murder of a popular girl whose body remains missing. You see, it's only Pippa who believes in Sal's innocence, and she will save the day, because she is a GOOD GIRL and Sal was once nice to her years ago! I was already annoyed at that point.<br><br>However, from there this story devolves into a sleuthing adventure where Pippa manages to have every Tom, Dick and Harry confess all their misdoings to her, because PIPPA IS WRITING A SCHOOL PAPER ABOUT THE MURDER. She catphishes people, breaks into houses, blackmails drug dealers, discovers 5-year old evidence in plain view, because she is just so much better than the police at everything. I can understand why police wouldn't care to pursue a case of a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Vandal" rel="nofollow noopener">Who Drew The D!cks or The Turd Bulrglar </a> variety, but a suicide and a presumed murder? And the victim is still missing and nobody but Pippa cares? Have you heard of Natalie Halloway? She disappeared 15 years ago, and she is still on TV. The whole investigation was one giant eyeroll for me.<br><br>Anyway, to put it short, this book has nothing that I look for in a mystery. I am not reading any more YA mysteries if suspending disbelief entirely is the main requirement to get through them. I am just going to stick with Courtney Summers from now on. Thankfully she has another one coming out next year, and it's about cults!<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/53138093.The_Project" title="The Project by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1589381478l/53138093._SY75_.jpg" alt="The Project by Courtney Summers" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="82620672639192399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Pip chooses the case for her senior project. She even tea</span>
  <span id="freeText4449215285606621477" style="display:none"><br /><br /><br />My reviews can also be seen at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com/">https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br /><br /><strong>A terrific Young Adult thriller! </strong><br /><br />Five years ago, Sal Singh murdered seventeen-year-old, Andie Bell.<br /><br />Or did he?<br /><br />The police, the press, and almost the whole town thought he did. And what he did after he was charged with the crime didn’t help change anyone’s mind.<br /><br />But Andie’s body was never found….<br /><br />Seventeen-year-old, Pippa (Pip) Fitz-Amobi isn’t so sure that Sal was guilty. Pip chooses the case for her senior project. She even teams up with Sal's brother, Ravi. Ravi believes his brother is innocent and desperately wants to clear his name.<br /><br />After receiving some threatening messages, it soon becomes clear that someone wants Pip to stop investigating and leave this "solved" case well enough alone.<br /><br />If Sal didn't kill Andie then who did? Pip could be in danger if a ruthless killer is still roaming the streets of Fairview.<br /><br /><strong>A complex and compelling story with a great cast of characters and loads of drama and tension. An excellent debut!<br /></strong><br /><br />I don't read a lot of young adult novels, but now and then I come across a winner!<br /><br />I was gripped by the fast-paced story and finished it in just a couple of days. Interspersed was mixed media including, transcripts, text messages, journal entries, that helped pull me even further into the story. Although I figured a few things out early on, I was still excited to see what was going to happen next.<br /><br /><strong>An addictive and captivating story of murder, deception, secrets, and obsession!</strong><br /><br />I'm really looking forward to reading the next book in this thrilling series by Holly Jackson.<br /><br /> <br /><br /> <br /><br /><strong> </strong><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17236934038878655105"><b>This was just phenomenal and I am most absolutely exhuasted.</b> In a good way?! I am totally draped over my bed marvelling at the author's intensely genius brain and how she put all this together (with all the twists and turns and red herrings and just plots within plots) and how satisfying it was to watch unravel. Reading the book was like when you start digging a hole at the beach, and more sand falls in and water appears and suddenly the hole is growing larger by itself and you're standing there</span>
  <span id="freeText17236934038878655105" style="display:none"><b>This was just phenomenal and I am most absolutely exhuasted.</b> In a good way?! I am totally draped over my bed marvelling at the author's intensely genius brain and how she put all this together (with all the twists and turns and red herrings and just plots within plots) and how satisfying it was to watch unravel. Reading the book was like when you start digging a hole at the beach, and more sand falls in and water appears and suddenly the hole is growing larger by itself and you're standing there with a teaspoon like :O<br /><br /><b>I don't want to give too much away of the plot!</b> But basically the premise is Pippa starts unravelling a cold case for a school project. Because, ya know, that's what you do for homework. She's an absolute A+ student, always perfect, so intensely intelligent, just sweet and brilliant really. But the further she gets into digging up this mystery (which, in their small town, is rather personal too and connected to many people she knows) the more she also sacrifices her "good girl" label. So even the TITLE is genius?!<br /><br />(Also shout out to Pip's family: a mixed family, her mum is white, her step-dad is Nigerian and her little brother Joshua is biracial, but Pip absolutely is just like FAMILY. And her dad and her relationship is so sweet?! It just added such a lovely layer. And also there were a few moments where Pip also acknowledged her white privilege and I just appreciate when books do this.)<br /><br /><b>Addictive, genius, compelling, and straight up chilling at times.</b> Although not particularly gory or macabre, so you can definitely go into it if you're new to thrillers. It's about intelligence and puzzles, but definitely incorporates a dark side. (I also appreciated it was about friendships, no romance!) The clues don't stop unravelling till the very last page and AH. I see a sequel. I want the sequel. Someone gently lower it into my hands and leave me leaking on the floor in pure admiration for this book.</span>

  <span id="freeText14762251688227303362" style="display:none">So here it is...unpopular opinion alert. Sorry guys I just didn't love it as much as pretty much everyone else in the world. <div id="review_2498010987" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Umut Rados" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24816039-umut-rados"><img alt="Umut Rados" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576844432p2/24816039.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2498010987?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Umut Rados" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Umut Rados" href="/user/show/24816039-umut-rados">Umut Rados</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2498010987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14270001798169272850">Rounded up from 4.5 stars. This is a YA crime thriller, and I enjoyed it so much! <br/>In a small town, 5 years ago, a young girl called Andie went missing and they could never find her. Her ex-boyfriend (Sal) is found dead just a few days later leaving solid proof that he did it and he took his own life. So, the police closes the case, and declared Sal as the murderer and Andie dead. <br/>5 years after, Pip, a brilliant student chooses the case as her homework. But, in her mind, she never believed Sal wa</span>
  <span id="freeText14270001798169272850" style="display:none">Rounded up from 4.5 stars. This is a YA crime thriller, and I enjoyed it so much! <br />In a small town, 5 years ago, a young girl called Andie went missing and they could never find her. Her ex-boyfriend (Sal) is found dead just a few days later leaving solid proof that he did it and he took his own life. So, the police closes the case, and declared Sal as the murderer and Andie dead. <br />5 years after, Pip, a brilliant student chooses the case as her homework. But, in her mind, she never believed Sal was guilty, so she's going to try to prove that. Who killed Andie? And where is she? <br /><br />First of all, this was way more complex and well built than I had expected because it's the debut of the author. It was gripping from the first page, I read it in 2 sittings (and it's 430 pages long!) I literally couldn't put it down. <br />It's written in a format that we see Pip's documentation for her homework, sometimes in diary format, sometimes maps, drawings or interviews with people she talked to. At other times, it's told from third person perspective to get the story moving. <br />I very much enjoyed this format, as it didn't make the book monotonous. It was interesting to treat it as a case, being solved in front of my eyes, and I did try to solve it :) <br />I had many scenarios going in my head, and figured out some, but certainly not fully. It was full of twists and turns until the last moment. I'll be honest, I could hear my heart beating at some points.<br />Another aspect I loved was the characters, Pip was a lot of fun. It was humorous at times. It didn't feel heavy hearted because of a murder case. No trigger warnings or any gritty details, which is a big plus for me. <br />Weren't there any 'coincidences' or 'conveniences'? Yes, there were. The book was a tad long, and maybe it'd be better if it was stripped down a few details. <br />BUT, as a whole, I sure enjoyed my time a lot. I don't mind the conveniences at all, as they were a very minor con compared to the thrilling sense I got from this book, and enjoyed my time. <br />I'd auto-buy Holly Jackson's next book for sure. <br />If you're looking for a good YA thriller, with a good chase and fun characters, don't miss this! And, if you enjoyed One Of Us Is Lying, you'll surely enjoy this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14270001798169272850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3507158428" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3507158428" />
    <a title="Unknown Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/116523065-unknown-reviews"><img alt="Unknown Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592560248p2/116523065.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3507158428?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Unknown Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Unknown Reviews" href="/user/show/116523065-unknown-reviews">Unknown Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3507158428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13769070705308890748"><b> 3.5 </b><br/><br/>I’m not someone who tends to read murder mysteries, but the good reviews and title had me intrigued. Suffice to say, I wasn’t let down.<br/><br/>In the town of Little Kilton, a schoolgirl named Andie Bell disappeared five years and was never found. Everyone knows her boyfriend, Sal, was the killer – after all he confessed and committed suicide a few days after she was reported missing. Yet Pippa Fitz-Amobi believes otherwise. For her final year project, she decides to investigate the case herself and</span>
  <span id="freeText13769070705308890748" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 </b><br /><br />I’m not someone who tends to read murder mysteries, but the good reviews and title had me intrigued. Suffice to say, I wasn’t let down.<br /><br />In the town of Little Kilton, a schoolgirl named Andie Bell disappeared five years and was never found. Everyone knows her boyfriend, Sal, was the killer – after all he confessed and committed suicide a few days after she was reported missing. Yet Pippa Fitz-Amobi believes otherwise. For her final year project, she decides to investigate the case herself and unravel what<i> really </i>happened to Andie. <br /><br />I loved the main character. <b> Pippa </b> is an over-achieving and witty seventeen-year-old who is motivated by her sense of justice. She’s the kind of person who knows the Latin for certain words, or the name of an obscure bird species. But I have to say, I really liked her. How she came to her conclusions were believable yet involved her thinking outside the boxes (logging into other account, emailing people as a fake journalist). She never grows overbearing, and while I do think she could be fleshed out more, I was rooting for her and her detective skills throughout the book. <br /><br />She is determined to exonerate Sal Singh of any crime, and seeks help in his younger brother, <b>Ravi</b>. Honestly, I adored Ravi as much as I did Pip and I think his suffering was another huge motivation for my need to see Pip succeed. Since his brother has been declared guilty, Ravi’s family has been harassed and shunned by the town community, including racial attacks due to their Indian heritage. He’s very funny and the chemistry between them was excellent. <br /><br />I think Jackson writes characters very well, but I do believe this book suffered from having a cast that was too large. At times, I was a little muddled on trying to remember who’s who. Now, I’m guessing since there’s apparently three sequels? in the making, she’s just setting up future pawns. This didn’t detract from the book overall, and since the characters that <i> were </i> focused on were really unique and intriguing, it’s a weak criticism of mine. <br /><br />Besides the characters, the plot was really fun to unwind. It’s told in a multimedia format, so we get both first person and third person perspectives. The little journal entries and audio interviews were great little snippets that kept me more engaged than I usually am. Also, eighty percent of the book moves at break neck speed, the kind of book that gets you to think “I’ll read just <i> one </i> more chapter,” only to realise you’ve finished another fifty pages. <br /><br />There’s a lot of twists in this book and not all of them are obvious (in my opinion). It’s really fun creeping into the twisted and dark secrets of some of the towns inhabitants, and there’s been a lot of storylines set up for the future. Even seeing Pippa lose some of her “good girl” persona was interesting to watch. She starts off this book as rather naïve, but grows more shady the deeper her investigation goes. <br /><br />(That said, while light-hearted and bubbly at times, this book does deal with many mature themes. I would recommend checking out trigger warnings before you decide to read this book.) <br /><br />I think the best way to describe this would to be a popcorn flick book, fast-paced and fun. Also,<b> there’s no romance!</b> There looks to be a future couple set up and I can’t wait to see if it goes through, but how I appreciate romance being devoid from the plot, especially one that takes place in a short time span. Pippa doesn’t have time for that. She’s even brushing off a guy who has a crush on her. Pippa has <b>real</b> problems (this is a stan Pippa post now, by the way) <br /><br />So where do my stars drop off? <br /><br />One <i>is</i> how the plot points come into place. Sometimes it’s pure luck, other times it’s a far fetched. Also some parts of this novel are a bit unrealistic. I do know it’s a teenager solving a murder and of course I should have some suspended belief, but threatening drug dealers or breaking into homes does kind of have me raising a few eyebrows. Also there are some things that Pippa discovered that I thought the police shouldn’t have missed. Since a body has never been found, I imagine the investigation wouldn’t necessarily be ongoing, but it wouldn’t have been forgotten about either. Maybe I’m being unfair applying true crime logic to a YA book, but a lot of this book involves factual logic used in real-life investigations. <br /><br />Two, none of the writing really stuck out to me, though it could be witty at times. This is obviously a very minor criticism compared to plot and characters, but it does feel like a debut. I’m not taking a star off for it though because it is good and YA is rather simple eighty percent of the time anyway. Also this wasn’t by any mean bad, just nothing special. <br /><br />Three is the ending. Now, I’m going to be fair; it was satisfying but I’d mark it down as a double ending. Half of it I thought was quite unrealistic and took me out of the book. The other half was who/what I predicted and the ended the novel very efficiently. So it had both a “safe” and an “unexpected” ending that fitted in the clues and backstories quite well, just one half felt too contrived. <br /><br /><b> Minor Mentions </b> <br /><br />I love how Pip’s family was in the background and supportive for a lot of the story. So many YA novels barely acknowledge parents. (Also Pip’s step-dad is Nigerian and her brother Joshua biracial, for those interested in diversity rep!)<br /><br /><b>This book really stands out to me a popcorn flick.</b> I think you can tell by the length of my review that there wasn’t much to the book, not enough to make it to my all-time favourites. This sounds like a criticism, but it really is just an enjoyable and quick read, I can’t stress it enough. I think this could even possibly be a beloved series and trendsetter for more mysteries in YA. <br /><br />Honestly, I wouldn’t buy the second book, on account of me being poor, but when it comes to my library, I’ll pick it up straight away. Also, 3.5 stars is seventy percent, which is pretty good. Almost as high as the Rotten Tomatoes score for The Prestige! It has Hugh Jackman!<br /><br />Really enjoyable read and I’d definitely recommend to anyone looking for a light and exciting book.<br /><br /><b> Conclusion:</b> This book is FUN! (Now go watch The Prestige)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13769070705308890748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It reminded me of when I was young and used to be obsessed with solving crimes in shows or Agatha Christie’s books and guessing the murderer right. <span id="freeTextContainer2013498072945690612">It’s been a while since I’ve picked up a YA mystery, and this one was very entertaining! Not only was it told through pose, but it also includes emails, transcripts, papers, etc. to make it feel as though you too are looking through piles of evidence to solve this local crime. It’s also been a while since I’ve read a book and didn’t successfully guess the plot twists, but one can also say the answer to this crime came somewhat out of no where, so *shrugs* I wasn’t utterly impressed by the ending</span>
  <span id="freeText2013498072945690612" style="display:none">It’s been a while since I’ve picked up a YA mystery, and this one was very entertaining! Not only was it told through pose, but it also includes emails, transcripts, papers, etc. to make it feel as though you too are looking through piles of evidence to solve this local crime. It’s also been a while since I’ve read a book and didn’t successfully guess the plot twists, but one can also say the answer to this crime came somewhat out of no where, so *shrugs* I wasn’t utterly impressed by the ending but I also wasn’t let down. I guess I was simply <i>satisfied</i> by it. <br /><br />In terms of narration, Pip’s logs, chronicling her ideas and theories as she solves this mystery, was in 1st person and the regular prose of the story being in 3rd person was a bit awkward to switch points of views so drastically, but it was still an enjoyable read. <br /><br />I also do have to call out how unethical Pip was while solving this mystery as well in terms of blackmailing suspects, breaking into homes to get evidence, impersonating a journalist, but I mean, that’s fiction for you. It truly be like that sometimes lol<br /><br />(ALSO WANT TO SAY SOMETIMES THREE STARS AREN’T A BAD THING. IT WAS FUN, ENTERTAINING, HAD ME ON MY TOES. I JUST DON’T HAVE TO GIVE EVERY BOOK I ENJOY FIVE STARS) <br /><br />TW: Sexual assault, drugs, roofies, death of a pet, kidnapping</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3277439364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7371622066713040516"><b>
  <i>"I just have to keep chasing, even when the path is resisting me."</i>
</b><br/><br/>The stakes are high, the suspect list is long, and threats are pouring in as Pippa digs up secrets that were supposed to be buried forever. If you're looking for a twisty, turn-y, can't put the book down type of mystery and haven't read <em>A Good Girl's Guide to Murder</em>... what are you waiting for?! This was such a fast paced, highly entertaining read that kept me on my toes for pretty much the entire book.<br/><br/><strong>What I Liked</strong><br/><br/>📓 <em>
  <strong>Format.</strong></em></span>
  <span id="freeText7371622066713040516" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"I just have to keep chasing, even when the path is resisting me."</i>
</b><br /><br />The stakes are high, the suspect list is long, and threats are pouring in as Pippa digs up secrets that were supposed to be buried forever. If you're looking for a twisty, turn-y, can't put the book down type of mystery and haven't read <em>A Good Girl's Guide to Murder</em>... what are you waiting for?! This was such a fast paced, highly entertaining read that kept me on my toes for pretty much the entire book.<br /><br /><strong>What I Liked</strong><br /><br />📓 <em>
  <strong>Format. </strong>
</em>I really enjoyed that this was told from Pippa's POV, journal-like entries for her capstone project, charts, and interviews with people who knew Andie around the time of her disappearance and death. I think it as a great way to make readers really present with Pip during her investigation and overall just the made it so much more of a compelling and engaging reading.<br /><br />🔀 <em><strong>Plot twists galore.</strong> </em>There are so many plot twists throughout this book and bombshells of revelations that will keep you on your toes almost the entire time. Some of the plot twists were shocking, others more predictable but either way it's very obvious to see that Pip is now in the middle of something much deeper than she could have ever possibly dreamed of.<br /><br />🧐 <em>
  <strong>A solid whodunnit.</strong>
</em> I definitely did not guess who the murderer was and that made for an even more exciting read in my opinion. A lot of times when it comes to mystery novels I figure out the killer or bad guy early on but the author gives us enough suspects, clues, and questions to keep your head spinning with possibilities all the way until the very end.<br /><br />💕 <strong>
  <em>Subtle Romance. </em>
</strong>I really liked the fact that although Pip and Ravi develop feelings for one another throughout their investigation it never becomes something that undermines what they're working towards and we only get to see a small out of romance between them at the very end. I really hate when mystery novels are overshadowed by romance, especially when we're working with a plot as complex as this one.<br /><br /><strong>What I Didn't Like</strong><br /><br />🐶 <em>
  <strong>Death of an animal. </strong>
</em>This has always been a hard limit for me and always will be. Aside from the simple of fact of just hating reading about it, I felt that it was so unnecessary to the plot. The murderer takes Pip's dog hostage and makes her hand over her laptop and research in exchange for her dog safe return, then releases the dog, and it dies on it's own? Like, come on. What was the point of that?<br /><br />🔚 <em>
  <strong>A little too abrupt.</strong>
</em> The ending of this came and went a little too quickly for me. There was a lot of action and revelations at the very end and majority of it was Pip realizing what happened and confronting the murderer about it. I definitely would have liked to see a little more of Pip piecing things together and not just running to the murderer for a confrontation.<br /><br />All in all,  if you're a fan of YA mystery/thrillers this should definitely earn a spot on your TBR. It's complex and intense while also fresh and exciting. I was super happy to see after finishing this that it's a series! Yes, this murder gets solved in this book and in the next book Pip and Ravi are on to solving a different case when a girl she knows goes missing. You better believe I'll be picking up the next one sooner rather than later!<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishchicksblog.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookishchick" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7371622066713040516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3372254656" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Lia Carstairs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75966379-lia-carstairs"><img alt="Lia Carstairs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605829031p2/75966379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3372254656?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lia Carstairs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lia Carstairs" href="/user/show/75966379-lia-carstairs">Lia Carstairs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75966379-lia-carstairs?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75966379-lia-carstairs?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75966379-lia-carstairs?shelf=all-time-fav">all-time-fav</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75966379-lia-carstairs?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3372254656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2860586578954163527"><b>Me reading the last few chapters..........</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595026039ra/29832746.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This was <b>bloody brilliant</b>! (Hehe, see what I did there😏)<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595032971ra/29832930.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Seriously though, why haven't I read this sooner? <br/>Aye, I know the answer to that. 'Twas me being hesitant and <b>stupid</b>. Fortunately, I changed that.😌<br/><br/>This is by far one of the <b>BEST</b> mystery books I've read this year. The suspense was <b>killing</b> me as I read and I was <i>
  <b>so tempted</b>
</i> to go to the back of the book and see who the culprit was.😅😁 Thankfully, I was able to squelch this urge and read until the en</span>
  <span id="freeText2860586578954163527" style="display:none"><b>Me reading the last few chapters..........</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595026039ra/29832746.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This was <b>bloody brilliant</b>! (Hehe, see what I did there😏)<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595032971ra/29832930.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Seriously though, why haven't I read this sooner? <br>Aye, I know the answer to that. 'Twas me being hesitant and <b>stupid</b>. Fortunately, I changed that.😌<br><br>This is by far one of the <b>BEST</b> mystery books I've read this year. The suspense was <b>killing</b> me as I read and I was <i>
  <b>so tempted</b>
</i> to go to the back of the book and see who the culprit was.😅😁 Thankfully, I was able to squelch this urge and read until the end without spoiling myself.<br><b>
  <u>Mission Accomplished😎</u>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595033446ra/29832947.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I absolutely <b>loved</b> Pip and Ravi. These days the mystery books I read have partners in crime. It's awesome with those two. Even when things got super dangerous and scary, they both still pushed on their investigation. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595034207ra/29832975.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Ravi</b> was super supportive and <b>Pip</b> is like one of the bravest and coolest MCs you can find. I mean, she spouts off random facts randomly and manages to get straight A's all while trying to uncover a dangerous case. <br><br><i>
  <b>‘My name is Pip and I know many things. I know that typewriter is the longest word that can be made with just one row of the keyboard. I know that the Anglo-Zanzibar war was the shortest in history, lasting only thirty-eight minutes.'</b>
</i><br><br>Also, even though almost everyone in town hated Ravi because of what Sal 'did', he didn't let that break him or change his belief that Sal wasn't the one who murdered Andie. <b>I love those two.🥰</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595034207ra/29832976.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ohmygod and when Pip finally uncovered who the actual murderer was and what really happened to Andie.......................<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595034703ra/29832992.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I <b>NEVER</b> IN A MILLION YEARS THOUGHT <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ELLIOT WARD WOULD BE THE MURDERER OF SAL AND BECCA BE THE MURDERER OF ANDIE?!?! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Totally didn't expect that. Like I suspected everyone but them.😨<br>And, you know, the sad thing is that it doesn't even feel like that much of a victory since <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[it kinda just destroyed two families even more; Becca's family already had Andie dead and Cara's family already had their mother dead, but now......it's even worse for them. Pretty sad, altho what Elliot and Bella did was still horrible. I feel more bad for Cara and Naomi.😢<br><br>MARK AND HOWIE TOTALLY GOT WHAT THEY DESERVED THOUGH. NEITHER DESERVE <b>MY PITY</b>👿 Mostly Mark, because he's a big jerk and so deserves to be sent to prison FOR LIFE.<br><br>Oh and I really am super suspicious of Stanley (that journalist) and Daniel (that young cop). I feel like they had something to do with the Andie Bell case, but who knows.......🤔 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Also, Pip's family was just like super cool. The dad, Victor, especially was hilarious and seeing his scenes in the book were the best.🤣<br><br><i>
  <b>Victor strolled over, wrapped his arm round her shoulders and squeezed. ‘Little Pipsy going to a house party.’<br>‘I know,’ Pip’s mum said, her smile wide and glistening. ‘With alcohol and boys.’<br>‘Yes.’ He let go and looked down at Pip, a serious expression on his face and his finger raised. ‘Pip, I want you to remember to be, at least, a little irresponsible.’<br>‘Right,’ Pip announced, grabbing her car keys and strolling to the front door. ‘We’re going now. Farewell, my backwards and abnormal parents.’<br>‘Fare thee well,’ Victor said dramatically, gripping on to the banister and reaching for the departing teenagers, like the house was a sinking ship and he the heroic captain going down with it.</b>
</i><br><br>I loved <b>A Good Girl's Guide to Murder</b> so much.💕 This would actually be a fitting end, but I'm so happy Holly Jackson has blessed us with more of her books with Pip as the MC. I want more of <b>The Adventures of Detective Pip and Ravi</b> (<s>Hmmm maybe Pavi or Rip</s>—nope forget I ever mentioned that😬😂)<br><br><b>
  <u>Note to self: DON'T <i>EVER</i> let me come up with ship names.</u>
</b><br><br><b>
  <u>Note to others: If you haven't, YOU <i>MUST</i> READ THIS BOOK.</u>
</b><br><br>Lia Carstairs ou—<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595036257ra/29833024.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://chainofnovels.wordpress.com/2020/07/18/a-good-girls-guide-to-murder-by-holly-jackson/" rel="nofollow noopener">|Blog|</a>

<div id="review_2818893454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2818893454" />
    <a title="Zoe Mann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65629974-zoe-mann"><img alt="Zoe Mann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557707575p2/65629974.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2818893454?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoe Mann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoe Mann" href="/user/show/65629974-zoe-mann">Zoe Mann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2818893454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7320029058389344576">Ok so I’ve had a full 24hours to get over how spectacular ‘A Good Girl’s Guide to Murder’ by Holly Jackson is and I now feel semi ready to write a review. <br/><br/>So where do I start, WOW, WOW, WOW! I needed this book. Reading had become so boring lately and this book slapped me right across the face and made me sit up straight and pay attention! <br/><br/>I loved everything about this book. The humour, the characters, the secrets, the emotions. I genuinely laughed out loud and burst out crying at this book (more</span>
  <span id="freeText7320029058389344576" style="display:none">Ok so I’ve had a full 24hours to get over how spectacular ‘A Good Girl’s Guide to Murder’ by Holly Jackson is and I now feel semi ready to write a review. <br /><br />So where do I start, WOW, WOW, WOW! I needed this book. Reading had become so boring lately and this book slapped me right across the face and made me sit up straight and pay attention! <br /><br />I loved everything about this book. The humour, the characters, the secrets, the emotions. I genuinely laughed out loud and burst out crying at this book (more than once!). My partner was beside me and asked why I was crying and when I told him he said he wished he hadn’t asked. <br /><br />IT’S THAT SAD and emotional and heart breaking BUT it’s also the most uplifting, heartwarming, totally fangirling novel, AND if that’s not enough it’s also a terrifying, edge of your seat, I’m scared to go to the toilet in the dark kind of story. Now do you understand why I couldn’t write the review yesterday? <br /><br />So what’s it about? Well, my totally awesome, geeky spirit animal Pippa aka Pip chooses a closed case to write and research for her end of year project. It’s an open and shut case as far as the town and police are concerned. 1 girl dead, murdered by her boyfriend, boyfriend panicked and killed himself before police could arrest him. The end! Pippa isn’t convinced though and when she acquires an unlikely “partner in crime” the two of them will stop at nothing to get to the truth. Even if it means putting themselves and their families in danger! <br /><br />This is a must read for everyone who enjoys a crime novel, psychological thriller, murder mystery, YA fiction, love story. It covers every genre and don’t let the YA category put you off. I am nearly 30 &amp; it is by far my favourite read this year. <br /><br />Can I finish by saying how amazing is the cover? It instantly caught my eye. I love it! <br /><br />Thank you to netgalley and the publisher for a free ARC in return for an honest review. This is going to be a best seller without a doubt! <br /><br />I WANT A NETFLIX SERIES!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7320029058389344576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
