<span id="freeTextContainer10854863988389073142">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>Welcome to this week’s episode of Conversations with Kelly and Mr. Kelly.<br/><br/>KELLY: Hey, get me THIS when you’re at Wal-Mart:<br/><br/><a href='https://lunapic.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>

  <span id="freeText10854863988389073142" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>Welcome to this week’s episode of Conversations with Kelly and Mr. Kelly.<br><br>KELLY: Hey, get me THIS when you’re at Wal-Mart:<br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589390519i/29469284._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>HUSBAND: Why do you need yarn? <br><br>KELLY: Don’t worry about it.<br><br>HUSBAND: I have the power this time around. I won’t buy it if you don’t tell me.<br><br>KELLY: I need it to make a murder board.<br><br>HUSBAND: What’s a . . . . . you know what? Never mind. I’ll get your yarn.<br><br>And then I went in for my one day in the actual office and made a murder board on my lunch break . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589390519i/29469283._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Now on to the book. Five years ago Andie Bell went missing and when her boyfriend Sal Singh promptly offed himself it was just assumed he did it and the case was closed, despite never finding Andie’s body. Pip chooses to take this unsolved mystery on as her senior project. She’s old enough to realize in most cases the simplest answer is the correct one (and, come on, the husband/boyfriend always did it, right?), she has some theories she wants to research in order to get an A and her shoe-in to early admission at Columbia. Said theories? <br><br>(1)	 <b>
  <i>“A third party killed Andie, but Sal was somehow involved, like an accessory after the fact, helped bury the body. His guilt leads him to suicide, and the evidence found on him implicates him as the perpetrator, even though he isn’t the one who killed her. The actual killer is still at large.”</i>
</b><br><br>(2)	<b>
  <i> “A third party killed Andie, and Sal had no involvement or awareness at all. His suicide days later wasn’t motivated by a murderer’s guilt, but maybe by a multitude of factors, including the stress of his girlfriend’s disappearance. The evidence found on him—the blood and the phone—have an entirely innocent explanation and are unrelated to her murder.” </i>
</b><br><br>(3)	<b>
  <i> “Andie is murdered by a third party on the Friday. The killer knows that Sal, as Andie’s boyfriend, would make the perfect suspect. Especially as Sal seems to have no alibi for over two hours that night. The killer murders Sal and makes it look like a suicide. They plant the blood and the phone on his body.” </i>
</b><br><br>(4)	<b>
  <i> “Theory four is the most far-fetched of the lot.” She took a deep breath and did it in one. “No one killed Andie Bell, because she isn’t dead. She faked her disappearance and then lured Sal out into the woods, murdered him, and dressed it up as a suicide. She planted her own phone and blood on him so that everyone believed she was dead. Maybe she needed to disappear for some reason.” </i>
</b><br><br>So there you have it in a nutshell. Are any of these theories close to being accurate? Or was the case truly as open and shut as the police believed?<br><br>I hate to say things like “for young adult, this was real good” because I read a lot of young adult and a lot of it is real good. That being said, this might be “real good” even for people who don’t generally pick up YA. The mystery was solid, as was the writing, the pacing was great and it didn’t get super Scooby Doo. Of course, the characters did put themselves in harm’s way like morons occasionally and didn’t face nearly as many obstacles obtaining information/putting two and two together as would likely happen in the real world, but hey it ain’t true crime so that can’t really be a complaint as far as I’m concerned. This required waaaaaay less suspension of disbelief than the majority of whodunits I’ve read.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1288009142570801685">OK... STANDING ovation for Holly Jackson friends. WOW this book totally blew my expectations out of the damn water plus some.<br/><br/>This book deserves all the stars plus more! I am SO unbelievably sad that this book had to come to an end.   <span id="freeText1288009142570801685" style="display:none">OK... STANDING ovation for Holly Jackson friends. WOW this book totally blew my expectations out of the damn water plus some.<br /><br />This book deserves all the stars plus more! I am SO unbelievably sad that this book had to come to an end. BUT, am SO ecstatic that this is going to a be a series and it looks like we only have to wait until April to get the second....muhahahahaahha.<br /><br />Easily one of my top thrillers of ALL time. Yes... ALL time. I can't tell you how refreshing it is as a huge thriller/mystery lover to come across a book like this that leaves you just breathless and in amazement for how much you loved it. <br /><br />What I loved most about this book was how it's written. The combination of interviews, journal entries, and project entries etc was brilliant. I absolutely loved the narrator Pippa and was instantly connected with her and the story. <br /><br />AND COME on THAT ending folks! DAMN. Ok... end of story go buy this ok? I had to purchase my own copy to put on my bright and shiny shelf because of how much I loved it.<br /><br />5 epic stars!<br /><br />Huge thank you to Netgalley and Delacorte Press for the arc in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />Pub date: 2/4/20<br />Published to GR/IG: 2/5/20</span>

        <a title="Jayme" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jayme" href="/user/show/11345366-jayme">Jayme</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5540286387706374587">3.5 rounded up! <br/><br/>I grew up reading the Nancy Drew (and lesser known, Trixie Belden) mystery series, so, I was curious to meet the newest 17 year old, sleuth, Pippa Fitz-Amobi! 🕵️‍♀️<br/><br/>But, if I was looking for a little NOSTALGIA , I would not be getting it here! <br/><br/>Nancy and Trixie were investigating in much more “innocent” times. <br/><br/>They didn’t have to deal with cell phones, burner phones, and social media. <br/>Sex, Drugs or Alcohol! <br/><br/>For her senior year Capstone project (like a thesis) Pippa decides to inves</span>
  <span id="freeText5540286387706374587" style="display:none">3.5 rounded up! <br /><br />I grew up reading the Nancy Drew (and lesser known, Trixie Belden) mystery series, so, I was curious to meet the newest 17 year old, sleuth, Pippa Fitz-Amobi! 🕵️‍♀️<br /><br />But, if I was looking for a little NOSTALGIA , I would not be getting it here! <br /><br />Nancy and Trixie were investigating in much more “innocent” times. <br /><br />They didn’t have to deal with cell phones, burner phones, and social media. <br />Sex, Drugs or Alcohol! <br /><br />For her senior year Capstone project (like a thesis) Pippa decides to investigate “What Really Happened to Andie Belle, a 17 year old who went missing from Fairview, Connecticut, and if her boyfriend was really guilty of murdering her...<br /><br />Though similar versions of Andie Bell’s life, (and disappearance) have been done many times, this YA novel tells this TYPE of tale through the unique approach of Pippa’s investigation -shared through Capstone Project Log entries, interviews and graphs. <br /><br />Because of this style, it’s a bit repetitious, but it’s still a fun read! <br /><br />I think that YA readers will enjoy solving this case with Pippa, and will look forward to seeing what mystery awaits her next!<br /><br />TRIGGER WARNING! 🐶 WHY, won’t these authors learn that we do NOT want to read about dogs and cats coming to harm!! ?? </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4590919748251513725">☾ ⋆.<br/>┊. ˚ ✦ 𝟰.𝟱/𝟱 <br/><br/>“𝗵𝗶𝘀𝘁𝗼𝗿𝘆’𝘀 𝗴𝗿𝗲𝗮𝘁𝗲𝘀𝘁 𝗺𝗶𝗻𝗱𝘀 𝗮𝗹𝘄𝗮𝘆𝘀 𝗮𝗱𝘃𝗶𝘀𝗲𝗱 𝗯𝗼𝗹𝗱 𝗼𝘃𝗲𝗿 𝘀𝗮𝗳𝗲; 𝘁𝗵𝗲𝗶𝗿 𝘄𝗼𝗿𝗱𝘀 𝗴𝗼𝗼𝗱 𝗽𝗮𝗱𝗱𝗶𝗻𝗴 𝗳𝗼𝗿 𝗲𝘃𝗲𝗻 𝘁𝗵𝗲 𝘄𝗼𝗿𝘀𝘁 𝗶𝗱𝗲𝗮𝘀.”<br/><br/><br/>RIGHT NOW, I really think I need to wear my coat and buy one of those murder boards with red strings and pins because I'M SO READY TO SOLVE THE CASE.<br/><br/>Me while reading this book (at first):<br/>*knock knock*<br/>Okay my lovely brain, who is the murderer? <br/>*my brain process* : failed, We don't access to all the evidence. Sorry! Please Try later.<br/>Me: I WANT TO KNOW!!! I WANT TO KNOW!! TEL</span>
  <span id="freeText4590919748251513725" style="display:none">☾ ⋆.<br />┊. ˚ ✦ 𝟰.𝟱/𝟱 <br /><br />“𝗵𝗶𝘀𝘁𝗼𝗿𝘆’𝘀 𝗴𝗿𝗲𝗮𝘁𝗲𝘀𝘁 𝗺𝗶𝗻𝗱𝘀 𝗮𝗹𝘄𝗮𝘆𝘀 𝗮𝗱𝘃𝗶𝘀𝗲𝗱 𝗯𝗼𝗹𝗱 𝗼𝘃𝗲𝗿 𝘀𝗮𝗳𝗲; 𝘁𝗵𝗲𝗶𝗿 𝘄𝗼𝗿𝗱𝘀 𝗴𝗼𝗼𝗱 𝗽𝗮𝗱𝗱𝗶𝗻𝗴 𝗳𝗼𝗿 𝗲𝘃𝗲𝗻 𝘁𝗵𝗲 𝘄𝗼𝗿𝘀𝘁 𝗶𝗱𝗲𝗮𝘀.”<br /><br /><br />RIGHT NOW, I really think I need to wear my coat and buy one of those murder boards with red strings and pins because I'M SO READY TO SOLVE THE CASE.<br /><br />Me while reading this book (at first):<br />*knock knock*<br />Okay my lovely brain, who is the murderer? <br />*my brain process* : failed, We don't access to all the evidence. Sorry! Please Try later.<br />Me: I WANT TO KNOW!!! I WANT TO KNOW!! TELL ME SOMETHING. <br />My brain: ERROR!! SHUT UP AND GO read the book yourself. I'm not a fortune teller or a detective, I'm just a poor organ who trys to endure your stupid self for living.<br /><br />*** okay, I'm going to stop this crazy talk with myself ***<br /><br />“𝗔𝗻𝗱 𝘁𝗵𝗼𝘂𝗴𝗵 𝘁𝗵𝗶𝘀 𝘀𝘁𝗼𝗿𝘆 𝗱𝗼𝗲𝘀 𝗵𝗮𝘃𝗲 𝗶𝘁𝘀 𝗺𝗼𝗻𝘀𝘁𝗲𝗿𝘀, 𝗜’𝘃𝗲 𝗳𝗼𝘂𝗻𝗱 𝘁𝗵𝗮𝘁 𝗶𝘁 𝗶𝘀 𝗻𝗼𝘁 𝗼𝗻𝗲 𝘁𝗵𝗮𝘁 𝗰𝗮𝗻 𝗯𝗲 𝘀𝗼 𝗲𝗮𝘀𝗶𝗹𝘆 𝗰𝗹𝗲𝗮𝘃𝗲𝗱 𝗶𝗻𝘁𝗼 𝘁𝗵𝗲 𝗴𝗼𝗼𝗱 𝗮𝗻𝗱 𝘁𝗵𝗲 𝗯𝗮𝗱. 𝗜𝗻 𝘁𝗵𝗲 𝗲𝗻𝗱, 𝘁𝗵𝗶𝘀 𝘄𝗮𝘀 𝗮 𝘀𝘁𝗼𝗿𝘆 𝗮𝗯𝗼𝘂𝘁 𝗽𝗲𝗼𝗽𝗹𝗲 𝗮𝗻𝗱 𝘁𝗵𝗲𝗶𝗿 𝗱𝗶𝗳𝗳𝗲𝗿𝗲𝗻𝘁 𝘀𝗵𝗮𝗱𝗲𝘀 𝗼𝗳 𝗱𝗲𝘀𝗽𝗲𝗿𝗮𝘁𝗶𝗼𝗻, 𝗰𝗿𝗮𝘀𝗵𝗶𝗻𝗴 𝘂𝗽 𝗮𝗴𝗮𝗶𝗻𝘀𝘁 𝗲𝗮𝗰𝗵 𝗼𝘁𝗵𝗲𝗿.”<br /><br />This book has all the elements and the things that the mystery books need and it'll keep you guessing until the end. <br /><br />➴ the book, the storyline and the plot twists set your heart on fire. And the effects and the impression it has on you is so beautiful. It teaches you so many important and valuable lessons for living.<br />➴ persons of interest list. ( I really liked this part!!) <br />➴ The way the evidence, the clues and the leads were developed and found.<br />➴ The unpredictable and emotional ending; it was so beautiful and heart breaking.<br />➴ the amazing storyline and plot. Everything was so good planned and related toghter. <br />➴ The perfect characters and best relationships. (I love Ravi; he was so cute.) <br />➴ when Mystery mixed with contemporary you are scared that it's getting boring after a while, but in this book it was written so well and it didn't make you want to stop reading it.<br />➴ The main character was such a clever, funny, lovely, and curious person. I mean every plan she had and every step she took to solve the case was great. (Sometimes she was annoying but no problem!) <br /> *whispering, she is my BABY girl!!*<br /><br /> ↬ most of the time when I read mystery books it's predictable and I can guess the killer, the leads and the clues or the way the murderer is found is not that impressive. but in this book it was a little hard to guess it, and it surprised me at the end. It was the best mystery book that I've ever read. From now on I'm a big fan of small town murder mystery books.<br /><br />So This book grabs your attention till the end and stucks you in the city full of so many secrets and mysterious things, and makes you feel like you are the detective and you must solve the case and follow every clue and lead that the murderer left behind. It was also so beautiful and emotional and made me want to cry.<br /><br />This book can teach you so many important things; your behavior can effect on your future and people around you. the way you act and every decision you made lead you to the future you can't predict. Be aware and be careful that your behavior and your decisions don't Hurt people's feelings or ruin their lives. Be responsible for what you do. think wisely before you act; because this is the real life not just the game to play with people's lives and souls. we talk about our lives, our souls and our hearts, so don't change this world to something disgusting, Somewhere that we can't even breath while living.<br /><br />𝔻𝕠𝕟'𝕥 𝕝𝕖𝕥 𝕥𝕙𝕚𝕤 𝕨𝕠𝕣𝕝𝕕 𝕓𝕠𝕣𝕟 𝕒𝕟𝕕 𝕔𝕣𝕖𝕒𝕥𝕖 𝕞𝕠𝕟𝕤𝕥𝕖𝕣𝕤, 𝕒𝕟𝕕 𝕥𝕣𝕪 𝕟𝕠𝕥 𝕥𝕠 𝕓𝕖 𝕥𝕙𝕖 𝕠𝕟𝕖 𝕨𝕙𝕠 𝕒𝕨𝕒𝕜𝕖𝕤 𝕥𝕙𝕖 𝕞𝕠𝕟𝕤𝕥𝕖𝕣𝕤 𝕚𝕟𝕤𝕚𝕕𝕖 𝕡𝕖𝕠𝕡𝕝𝕖. <br /><br />My personal thoughts: <br /> I can honestly say it was the first book that I couldn't guess who was the murdere at first. Actually in this book I wrote my own persons of interest list about the murderer and guess what? <br />I COULD GUSEE THE KILLER!! (ERRRRR...GGZZZZ)<br />at the end of the book I was like " I knew it!! I knew it!!! I knew it!!!! (As if I was on stage and I won the Grammy award for the most clever detective in the world. *hahahah just kidding!!*)</span>

<div id="review_3069784834" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3069784834" />
    <a title="Katie B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49444196-katie-b"><img alt="Katie B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469412116p2/49444196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3069784834?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie B" href="/user/show/49444196-katie-b">Katie B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781984896360" href="/book/show/45874065-a-good-girl-s-guide-to-murder">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=connecticut">connecticut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3069784834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15718368425408263533">4.5 stars<br/><br/>This book has been out for awhile now so I was aware of all the hype surrounding it. I have to say it lived up to it. A fun mystery to read because it felt like I was right along with the main character trying to solve the case like I'm some amateur detective.<br/><br/>Five years ago tragedy struck the town of Fairfield. High school senior, Andie Bell was murdered by her boyfriend, Sal Singh. Days later, Sal committed suicide.<br/><br/>Pip is currently a senior in high school and she's always had some doub</span>
  <span id="freeText15718368425408263533" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />This book has been out for awhile now so I was aware of all the hype surrounding it. I have to say it lived up to it. A fun mystery to read because it felt like I was right along with the main character trying to solve the case like I'm some amateur detective.<br /><br />Five years ago tragedy struck the town of Fairfield. High school senior, Andie Bell was murdered by her boyfriend, Sal Singh. Days later, Sal committed suicide.<br /><br />Pip is currently a senior in high school and she's always had some doubts about Sal being the killer. So she decides to reexamine the case as part of a school project. By interviewing people who were close to Andie and Sal, Pip comes up with some interesting leads. The more Pip digs for the truth, the more it becomes an obsession.<br /><br />What I loved about reading this book, is I would start to feel confident about a theory as to what happened and then the author would pull the rug out from under me and I would have to go back to the drawing board. It's like she enjoyed toying with the reader. Sadly, I am no modern day Nancy Drew because all I was able to do was recognize a few key things that I had a feeling would factor into the story later on. I certainly was not able to come up with a logical explanation as to why the things were important though. The story is complicated and kudos to any Sherlock Holmes type readers that are able to put it all together before the big reveal. <br /><br />I highly recommend this book even if you don't normally read YA fiction. It's an entertaining mystery and I look forward to seeing if the sequel to the book is just as good.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15718368425408263533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('A3WrmAoH62EOa6zy1aCQZ9/b25NaSPgBv7tEGUtlkz5KPCkDLy/9YN46LH2bxTXOW/XTjEllMKOglJCSs7IIAA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3ZTVRDv5oW5qebWVi62D5YcD57/SMeyioiuZBephpouU3VffHtG3b7ooNRrFyCZMAy3voMEcJAC9BE2OErY9tQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3085664987072107794">Holly Jackson was born in 1992. She grew up in Buckinghamshire and started writing stories from a young age, completing her first (poor) attempt at a book aged fifteen. <br/><br/>'A Good Girl's Guide to Murder' is a YA Mystery Thriller and her debut novel. She lives in London and aside from reading and writing, she enjoys binge-playing video games and pointing out grammatical errors in street signs.</span>
